RT @pistoleraprod: Delegation from @amnestyusa expected to arrive at #border this week.	‚ÄúWhile President Trump continues to  fight for a bo‚Ä¶
It demonstrates the lengths Mexico and the US will take to violate the human rights of people, including children, desperately seeking safety.
Yesterday‚Äôs standoff with Mexican officials validates reports that authorities there are cooperating with the US to dissuade people from asking for asylum.
Over an hour later, our director @MargaretLHuang was able to negotiate an agreement w/ Mexican authorities. She &amp; an interpreter would accompany the children onto US soil to ask for asylum if the rest of the delegation left. The children were then processed &amp; made it into the US.
The delegation refused to leave until the children were allowed to present their claims. In order to discourage the delegation to leave, Mexican authorities asked everyone with proper documents to proceed through the port of entry while the delegation stood to the side.
In any case, minors are not allowed to put their name on this list. Children have no choice but to present their claims at the port of entry.
In doing so, they exert influence over the manager of the list while avoiding accusations of metering. This practice is not only unconscionable, it is against international law.
According to reports from organizations on the ground, Mexican authorities select asylum-seekers to keep the list for weeks at a time by promising them they will be able to cut the line.
The authorities claimed that asking for asylum at the port of entry is against proper procedure and advised the children to get on the asylum waitlist. The authorities also claimed that the asylum waitlist is kept in an informal notebook managed by the asylum-seekers themselves.
Upon approaching the port of entry, the delegation was stopped by Mexican authorities who refused to allow the children to proceed any further to present their asylum claims.

We have asked repeatedly Twitter to make available meaningful and comprehensive data regarding the scale and nature of abuse on their platform, as well as how they are addressing it. #ToxicTwitter
In our sample study, black women were disproportionately targeted, being 84% more likely than white women to be mentioned in abusive or problematic tweets. #ToxicTwitter
Women of color, (black, Asian, Latinx and mixed-race women) were 34% more likely to be mentioned in abusive or problematic tweets than white women. #ToxicTwitter
Using a combination of data science, machine learning, and thousands of volunteers to survey millions of tweets, we found that 7.1% of tweets sent to the women in the study were problematic or abusive. #ToxicTwitter
We partnered with an artificial intelligence software product company, called Element AI (@element_ai), using a sample of tweets mentioning 778 politicians and journalists in the US as well as in the UK. #ToxicTwitter

"If Mexico agrees to do the U.S. government‚Äôs dirty work at the expense of the caravan members‚Äô dignity and human rights, it is effectively paying for Trump‚Äôs shameful border wall." - @ErikaGuevaraR, Americas Director at @amnesty
We received reports from Mexican officials speaking anonymously that raise doubts as to the supposed lack of capacity by US authorities to receive more people and indicate the pressure that the US government exercises on Mexican authorities to restrict entry of asylum seekers.
Yet our researchers confirmed with multiple sources in the Mexican government that Mexican immigration officials routinely take possession of the waitlist each night, and coordinate with U.S. border authorities on how many asylum seekers from the list will be received each day.
Mexican authorities cannot lawfully prevent people from exiting the country and seeking asylum at the U.S. border. #CaravanaMigrante
Mexican federal, state and municipal officials separately confirmed to our researchers that the temporary shelter did not have sufficient food, water and health services, and that respiratory illnesses were spreading among those staying there. #CaravanaMigrante
On November 18, our researchers visited Tijuana‚Äôs Benito Juarez sports complex, a temporary shelter where the municipal government had accommodated approximately 3,000 migrants and asylum seekers who had arrived in the first of several caravans totaling 8,000 -10,000 people.
Instead of militarizing the border &amp; peddling fear &amp; discrimination, Trump‚Äôs administration should show compassion for those forced to flee their homes &amp; must receive their requests for asylum without delay as required by US &amp; international law - @ErikaGuevaraR of @amnesty
Conditions could only worsen under a reported deal between both countries that, if agreed, would force asylum-seekers to remain in Mexico while their claims are processed, rather than allow them to enter the United States. #CaravanaMigrante
Unlawful U.S. border policies are leaving thousands of asylum seekers stranded in Mexico, where they are facing threats of deportation to their countries of origin, where they potentially face serious harm. #CaravanaMigrante
